section 1 multiple dwelling means any trailer designed and intended to accommodate more than one family 2 park means trailer coach park 3 trailer coach means any portable structure or vehicle so constructed and designed as to permit occupancy thereof for dwelling or sleeping purposes for one family 4 trailer coach park means any plot of ground upon which two or more trailer coaches occupied for dwelling or sleeping purposes are located regardless of whether or not a charge is made for such accommodation 5 trailer coach space means a plot of ground available to an owner for use as a site for a trailer coach cross reference definitions and rules of construction generally  12 b parks prohibited it shall be unlawful for any person to maintain or operate within the limits of the town any multiple dwelling any park or any trailer coach park within the contemplation of this section c license for coaches required  fee it shall be unlawful for any person to maintain or operate any trailer coach unless such person shall first obtain a license therefor the license fee for each trailer coach shall be $2500 d applications for coach licenses application for a trailer coach license shall be filed with and issued by the board of selectmen applications shall be in writing signed by the applicant accompanied by the license fee and shall contain the following 1 the name and address of the applicant  2 the location and legal description of the trailer coach  3 the description of the trailer coach space to be used exclusively for the site of said trailer coach the lot site for the trailer shall be not less than 5000 square feet where it is served by a public sewer system and a public water supply and not less than 25000 square feet on a lot not less than 100 feet wide where it is not served by a public sewer system and a public water supply  4 that the applicant has title to the trailer coach and also to the trailer coach space to be used as a site  5 that the applicant will conform to all municipal and state ordinances and laws existing pertaining to health sanitation nuisance and fire e revocation  reissuance of coach licenses the board of selectmen may revoke any license to maintain and operate any trailer coach when the licensee has been found guilty by a court of competent jurisdiction of violating any provision of this section after such conviction the license may be reissued if the circumstances leading to the conviction have been remedied f penalty any person violating the provisions of this section shall be fined no more than $2500 for each offense each day that a violation is permitted to exist shall constitute a separate offense  blasting a preblast inspections 1 whenever blasting operations are to be conducted within 200 feet of a structure which is neither owned nor leased by the project contractor or the blaster the following precautions shall be adhered to a a preblast inspection of all structures within 200 feet range shall be conducted  b the inspection shall include both interior and exterior visible and accessible areas  c the inspection record shall be available for inspection by the owner of the structure a copy of said report shall be forwarded to the fire marshals office at least three working days prior to blasting operations 2 the requirements of this section shall be considered satisfied under the following conditions a if three unsuccessful attempts have been made to notify the owneroccupant of the structure  b if the inspection or access to the structure is refused by the owneroccupant and a signed waiver is obtained  c in the event that a signed waiver is not obtained notification shall be given to the owneroccupant of his rights via certified mail return receipt requested  3 the fire marshals office shall be notified of any structure which has not been inspected 4 the fire marshal or his representative may at his discretion at any time he deems necessary due to specific circumstances waive reduce or expand the area or structures required to be inspected b postblast inspections in the event of a complaint as stated in paragraph d postblast surveys shall be conducted in accordance with the requirements set forth under paragraph a1 4 and the results filed with the fire marshal or his representative within 60 days after said completion c application for blasting 1 the contractorblaster shall complete a state approved blasting application in the fire marshals office an application fee set by the board of selectman shall also be submitted with said application 2 the application will be for specific locations in a major construction project many blasting locations may be required and each site must have a separate blasting permit 3 the contractorblaster shall discuss the possibilities of using jack hammering or other types of less dangerous charges than dynamite with the fire marshal or his representative before the issuance of a permit and shall comply with these requirements where possible 4 the contractorblaster shall place warning signs of impending blasting on site at least 24 hours prior to commencing blasting activity d insurance requirements 1 the contractorblaster shall provide a certificate of insurance prior to the issuance of a blasting permit 2 the insurance certificate shall provide for blasters liability coverage and should be a specific certificate for blasting operations conducted in seymour 3 a minimum coverage limit to be provided is $100000000 and this amount may be expanded at the fire marshals discretion based upon the amount of blasting to be conducted and area in which it will take place e blasting damage complaints 1 any person firm or corporation alleging personal injury or property damage as a result of blasting operations shall make a written complaint to the fire marshal or his representative 2 the complaint shall include a date time location of incident  b description of injury or property damage  c name address signature of complainant and date of complaint  d name of blastercontractor if known 3 upon receipt of the complaint the fire marshal or his representative shall notify and require the blastercontractor to whom the blasting permit was issued to pick up and sign a copy of the complaint form 4 within 30 days of being notified the blastercontractor shall make a proper response to the complainant 5 the fire marshal or his representative shall conduct an investigation into the allegations made in the complaint upon finding that there has been a violation of this section or state regulations he may take whatever necessary to insure the public safety f precautions 1 the blaster shall take special precautions in the loading delaying initiation andor confinement of each blast with mats or other methods so as to control the throw of fragments and thus prevent bodily injury or property damage 2 the blaster shall provide approved seismic instrumentation to determine the actual magnitude of ground vibration the operation shall be operated by a qualified person and the recordings shall be interpreted by a qualified person the instrument shall be calibrated in accordance with the manufacturers recommendation the fire marshal or his representative may on his own initiation and the expense of the contractorblaster order the use of such instrumentation conducted by a professional service 3 the blaster shall abide by any other requirements as specified on the permit application by the fire marshal or his designee these may include but are not limited to designing the first blast to a scale distance of 70 providing extra seismic monitoring and notification to the fire marshal prior to blasting etc g definitions 1 structure for the purposes of preblast inspection surveys structures intended for a full inspection would be those found to be normally occupied other structures such as sheds wells inground pools etc shall be documented in the report as to their locations on the property being inspected h penalties any person in violation of any of the provisions in this article shall be deemed guilty of a misdemeanor and upon conviction thereof shall be fined in the amount not to exceed $20000 each day such violation continues after the time for correction of the violation has been given in an order shall constitute a continuing violation and the amount of the fine shall be doubled for each day the violation continues such fine not to exceed $80000 per day    massage parlors a definitions unless the particular provision or the context otherwise requires the definitions and provisions contained in this subsection shall govern the construction meaning and application of words and phrases used in this section 1 employee means any person over 18 years of age other than a masseur who renders any service in connection with the operation of a massage business and receives compensation from the operator of the business or patrons 2 massage means any method of treating the superficial parts of a patron for medical hygienic exercise or relaxation purposes by rubbing stroking kneading tapping pounding vibrating or stimulating with the hands or any instrument or by the application of air liquid or vapor baths of any kind whatsoever 3 masseur means any person who engages in the practice of massage as herein defined the use of the masculine gender shall include in all cases the feminine gender as well 4 patron means any person over 18 years of age who receives a massage under such circumstances that it is reasonably expected that he or she will pay money or give any other consideration therefor 5 recognized school means any school or institution of learning which has for its purpose the teaching of the theory method profession or work of massage which school requires a resident course of study of not less than 70 hours before the student shall be furnished with a diploma or certificate of graduation from such school following the successful completion of such course of study or learning b permits required 1 business permit no person shall engage in or carry on the business of massage unless he has a valid massage business permit issued by the town pursuant to the provisions of this section for each and every separate office or place of business conducted by such person 2 masseurs permit no person shall practice massage as a masseur employee or otherwise unless he has a valid and subsisting masseurs permit issued to him by the town pursuant to the provisions of this section c application for massage business permit any person desiring a massage business permit shall file written application with the police chief on a form to be furnished by the police chief the applicant shall partnership corporation or otherwise  2 the name style and designation under which the business or practice is to be conducted  3 the business address and all telephone numbers where the business is date of the application  4 the applicant has knowingly made any false misleading or fraudulent statement of fact in the permit application or in any document required by the town in conjunction therewith  5 the applicant has had a massage business masseur or other similar permit or license denied revoked or suspended for any of the above causes by the town or any other state or local agency within five years prior to the date of the application  6 the applicant if an individual or any of the officers and directors if the applicant is a corporation  or any of the partners if the applicant is a partnership  and the manager or other person principally in charge of the operation of the business is not over the age of 18 years  and 7 the manager or other person principally in charge of the operation of the business has not successfully completed a resident course of study or learning of not less than 70 hours from a recognized school where the theory method profession or work of massage is taught g display of permits the massage business permittee shall display his permit and that of each and every masseur employed in the establishment in an open and conspicuous place on the premises of the massage business h fee the permit fee for a massage business shall be $5000 per year or any part thereof the permit fee for masseurs shall be $1000 per year or any part thereof i revocation or suspension of permit any massage business or masseurs permit issued under this section shall be subject to suspension or revocation by the police chief for violation of any provision of this section or for any grounds that would warrant the denial of issuance of such permit in the first place the chief upon such revocation or suspension shall state his reasons in writing specifying the particular grounds for such revocation or suspension j keeping of records every person who operates a massage business or practices or provides a massage shall at all times keep an appointment book in which the name of each and every patron shall be entered together with the time date and place of service and the services provided such appointment book shall be available at all times for inspection by the police chief or his authorized representatives k transfers prohibited no massage business and masseur permits are transferable separate or divisible and such authority as a permit confers shall be conferred only on the permittee named therein l sanitation and safety requirements all premises used by permittees hereunder shall be periodically inspected by the police chief or his authorized representatives for safety of the structure and adequacy of plumbing ventilation heating and illumination the walls shall be clean and painted with washable moldresistant paint in all rooms where water or steam baths are given floors shall be free from any accumulation of dust dirt or refuse all equipment used in the massage operation shall be maintained in a clean and sanitary condition towels linen and items for personal use of operators and patients shall be clean and freshly laundered towels cloths and sheets shall not be used for more than one patron heavy white paper may be substituted for sheets provided that such paper is changed for every patron no massage service or practice shall be carried on within any cubicle room booth or any area within a massage establishment which is fitted with a door capable of being locked nothing contained herein shall be construed to eliminate other requirements of statute or ordinance concerning the maintenance of premises nor to preclude authorized inspection thereof m supervision a permittee shall have the premises supervised at all times when open for business any business rendering massage services shall have one person who qualifies as a masseur on the premises at all times while the establishment is open the permittee shall personally supervise the business and shall not violate or permit others to violate any applicable provision of this section the violation of any such provision by any agent or employee of the permittee shall constitute a violation by the permittee n persons under age 18 prohibited on the premises no person shall permit any person under the age of 18 years to come or remain on the premises of any massage business establishment as masseur employee or patron unless such person is on the premises on lawful business o alcoholic beverages prohibited no person shall sell give dispense provide or keep or cause to be sold given dispensed provided or kept any alcoholic beverage on the premises of any massage business p exceptions the provisions of this section shall not apply to hospitals nursing homes sanitariums ymcas ywcas or health clubs performing similar services and providing programs similar to those of the ymca and ywca or persons holding an unrevoked certificate to practice the healing arts under the laws of the state or persons working under the direction of any persons or in any such establishment nor shall this section apply to barbers or cosmetologists lawfully carrying out their particular profession or business and holding a valid unrevoked license or certificate of registration issued by the state q penalties any person violating any of the provisions of this section upon conviction shall be punished in accordance with section 19 reserved the said snap lock or doors from said icebox refrigerator or container  loitering a definitions the following words terms and phrases when used in this division shall have the meanings ascribed to them in this section except where the context clearly indicates a different meaning to loiter means standing around moving slowly about spending time idly sauntering delaying lingering or lagging behind b in public areas prohibited it shall be unlawful for any person to loiter on the streets sidewalks crosswalks walks in public parks or any other public area so as to impede and interfere with the use of the street sidewalk crosswalk walk in a public park or other public area by any other person any policeman may order any person violating this section to cease and desist from interfering with the right of any other person to use the streets sidewalks crosswalks walks in public parks or any other public area c loitering on school grounds prohibited a person having no reason or relationship involving custody of or responsibility for a pupil or any other license or privilege to be there shall not loiter on school grounds within the town during school hours or during those hours from dusk unless authorized by the school administrator or his duly authorized designee d on private property prohibited it shall be unlawful for any person to loiter on private property within the town without lawful business thereon or if ordered to quit the property by the owner thereof or his agent e penalties any person violating any of the provisions of this article shall be deemed guilty of a misdemeanor and upon conviction thereof shall be fined in an amount of $5000 dollars for the first offense and $10000 for each offense thereafter   2 sameoperation of motor vehicles on amended from time to time host shall mean to organize a gathering of two or more persons or to allow the premises under ones control to be used with ones knowledge for a gathering of two or more persons for personal social or business interaction minor shall have the same meaning as the same term is defined in title 30  301 of the connecticut general statutes as amended from time to time b possession no minor shall be in possession of alcoholic liquors whether in opened or closed containers or otherwise within the town of seymour except when accompanied by or in the presence of his or her parent guardian or spouse who has attained the age required to possess alcoholic liquors these restrictions shall apply to both public and private property c hosting events no person shall host an event or gathering at which the host knowingly allows alcoholic liquor to be consumed by or dispensed to any minor unless said minor is accompanied by or in the presence of his or her parent guardian or spouse who has attained the age required to possess consume or dispense alcoholic liquors this restriction shall apply to any event or gathering within the town of seymour whether conducted on public or private property d penalty any persons violating any provision of this act shall be subject to a fine of $9900 and any person under the age of 16 shall be referred to juvenile court   3 short title this section shall be known and may be cited as an ordinance regulating burglar holdup and fire alarm systems and users b purpose and definitions 1 the purpose of this section is to provide minimum standards and regulations applicable to burglar holdup and fire alarm users as defined in this section and to encourage the installation of protective alarm systems in all dwellings commercial industrial and agricultural structures 2 for the purpose of this section the following terms phrases words and their derivations shall have the meaning given herein when not inconsistent with the context words used in the present tense include the future words used in the plural number include the singular number and words in the singular include the plural number the word shall is always mandatory and not merely directory alarm agent means any person employed by an alarm business whose duties include the altering installing maintaining moving repairing selling servicing responding to or causing others to respond to an alarm device alarm business means any business operated by a person for a profit which engages in the activity of altering installing leasing maintaining moving repairing replacing selling servicing or responding to a burglar holdup or fire alarm system or which causes any of these activities to take place alarm system means an assembly of equipment and devices arranged to signal the presence of a hazard requiring urgent attention and to which police or fire are expected to respond in this section the term alarm system shall include the terms automatic holdup alarm system burglar alarm systems holdup alarm systems and manual holdup alarm systems alarm systems which monitor temperature humidity or any other condition not directly related to the detection of an unauthorized intrusion into a premises or an attempted robbery or a fire or smoke condition at a premises is to be included in this section alarm user means any person on whose premises or property an alarm system is maintained within the town annunciator means the instrumentation on an alarm console at the receiving terminal of a signal line which or audible signals announces when an alarm device at a particular location has been activated or it may also indicate line trouble automatic dialing device refers to an alarm system which automatically sends over regular telephone lines by direct connection or otherwise a prerecorded voice message or coded signal indicating the existence of the emergency situation that the alarm system is designed to detect burglar alarm system refers to an alarm system signaling an entry or attempted entry into the area protected by the system fire alarm system refers to a signal or message from a person or device indicating the existence of a fire or other emergency which requires fire department action town means the town of seymour connecticut direct connect means an alarm system which has the capability of transmitting system signals to and receiving them at an agency maintained by the local government for example a police communication center direct line means a telephone line leading directly to the communication center of an agency maintained by the local government that is only to report emergency signals false alarm means the activation of an alarm system failure malfunction improper installation or the negligence of the owner or lessee of an alarm system or of his employees or agents such terminology does not include for example alarms caused by hurricanes tornadoes earthquakes violent weather conditions or other acts of god false fire alarms shall not mean alarms transmitted because of a water main break or similar causes that occur outside of the protected property false alarms as defined in this section also do not include those alarms that are transmitted with a criminal malicious or mischievous intent holdup alarm system refers to an alarm signaling a robbery or attempted robbery in which the signal transmission is initiated by the direct action of the person attacked or by an observer of the attack person means any person firm partnership association corporation company or organization of any kind police chief means the chief of the police department of the town of seymour police or police department means the police department of the town of seymour fire marshal means the certified person designated as fire marshal by the town of seymour or his designated representative fire department means those volunteer companies authorized by the town of seymour to provide fire protection services subscriber means a person who buys andor leases or otherwise obtains an alarm signaling system and thereafter contracts with or hires an alarm business to monitor andor service the alarm device telephone company means the utility that furnishes telephone services to the town of seymour c direct connections to the seymour police department any direct line or automatic dialing device that terminates in the seymour police department communications center is prohibited d equipment maintenance each alarm user at his expense is required to maintain all components of the alarm system in good working order at all times to insure that the sensory mechanisms used in connection with such device be adjusted so as to suppress false indications of holdups or intrusions or fire or smoke conditions so that the device will not be activated by impulses due to short flashes of light wind rain noises vehicular noises or other forces unrelated to genuine alarms e requirements 1 no alarm system shall be installed by any person other than a licensed person or other person meeting the requirements as set forth in the building and electrical codes of the state no alarm system shall be installed unless an electrical permit to install the same has been obtained from the building official or his designee as required by the building and electrical codes of the state 2 all alarm systems which sound an audible signal which may be heard from the outside of the protected premises shall be equipped with a device which shall limit the duration of such audible sound to not more than 30 minutes or to such other length of time as may be required from time to time by the state department of environmental protection f enforcement 1 enforcement and administration of this section shall be the function of the police chief in the case of burglar and holdup alarms and the fire marshal in the case of fire alarms or their designee and shall be accomplished as provided in the following subsections 2 there are hereby imposed the following penalties upon an alarm user whose system transmits a false alarm a for the first two false alarms within any twelve month period  no action b for the third such alarm  written notice after the third such alarm the alarm user will receive a written notification of the third false alarm from the police chief or fire marshal the alarm user shall have five days from the date he receives the notification to correct the problem with the system and shall notify the police chief or fire marshal in writing of such correction the fiveday period shall exclude saturdays sundays and holidays there shall be no charge for false alarms occurring within the fiveday period nor shall such alarms be considered in determining penalties in accordance with this section c upon receipt of the fourth false alarm the town shall charge a penalty of $10000 for the fourth false alarm and each false alarm thereafter in any one calendar year 3 notwithstanding the provisions of subsection f2 there shall be no charge for the first alarm occurring within 30 days after the installation of an alarm system and such false alarm shall not be considered in determining penalties in accordance with the schedule set forth in subsection f2 4 failure of any alarm user andor alarm business or alarm agent supplier to comply with the requirements of a written notice of a violation of any provision hereof within five days of receipt of such notice exclusive of saturday sunday and holidays shall also constitute an offense punishable by a fine not to exceed $10000 such notice shall continue in force and effect until full compliance with requirements stated therein and each and every failure to comply with such notice within 24 hours after the five days allowed for compliance shall constitute a separate offense and stated fine shall be imposed for each offense g alarm user identification 1 immediately upon installation of an alarm system the police department shall be furnished in writing the following information name address and telephone number of the alarm user and any other person authorized in an emergency to gain access to the protected area a minimum of two names addresses and phone numbers shall be supplied in addition the alarm company who installed the system or is maintaining the system or monitors the system shall be supplied in accordance with this section 2 it shall be the responsibility of each alarm user to notify in writing the police department with any changes in the list 3 each commercial and financial institution within the town shall notify the police department in writing within 30 days after the effective date of this section h liability of the town of seymour the town shall not be liable for any defects in operation of any signal line system for any failure or neglect to respond appropriately upon receipt of an alarm from such source for any failure or neglect of any person in connection with the installation operation disconnection or removal of equipment the transmission of alarm signals or the relaying of such signals or messages  15   1 2   17   cross reference fire prevention and protection ch 6 intentional false alarms if any person shall knowingly give a false alarm of fire in the town or knowingly proclaim that a fire is extinguished when it is not such person shall be fined $25000 upon conviction    secs 11231140  reserved article ii  graffiti ordinance graffiti a definitions for the purpose of this article the following terms shall have the following meanings graffiti any letters numbers word or words writings or inscriptions symbols drawings carvings stickers etchings or any other marking of any nature whatsoever which defaces obliterates covers alters damages or destroys the real or personal property of another this chapter shall not be construed to prohibit easily removable chalk markings on public sidewalks and streets used in connection with traditional childrens games broad tipped indelible markers any felt marker or similar implement containing a fluid that is not water soluble and which has a flat or angled writing surface greater than a quarter of an inch wide b prohibited acts 1 no person shall write paint or place any paint chalk or any other substance or substances or otherwise mark scratch place carve or etch graffiti on the real or personal property of another whether said real or personal property be publicly or privately owned unless the owner of such property has specifically consented to the same prior to the commission of such act or acts 2 no person shall carry an aerosol spray paint can or broad tipped indelible marker or other marking devices into any public building or other public facility with the intent to violate the provisions of this or any other ordinance c violations and penalties any person violating any provision of this article shall be punished by a fine of 100 dollars  sale of aerosol cans and markers to minors prohibited a purpose the purpose of this section is to deter the defacing of public and private property use of aerosol spray paint cans broad tipped indelible markers and other marking devices within the town the sale of such aerosol spray paint cans and broad tipped indelible markers and other marking devices to a person under 18 years of age is prohibited b prohibited acts 1 no person shall sell offer to sell or otherwise transfer an aerosol spray paint can or broad tipped indelible marker or other marking devices to any person under 18 years of age unless such person is accompanied by a parent or guardian at the time of purchase 2 no person shall sell or offer for sale or otherwise transfer an aerosol spray paint can or broad tipped indelible marker or other marking devices unless such aerosol spray paint can or indelible marker or other marking devices are held for sale or transfer in an enclosed device which is constructed to prevent removal of the merchandise except by authorized attendants or is stored out of sight in such a way as to prevent free access to the merchandise by the public c violations and penalties any person who violates the any provision of this article shall be punished by a fine of 100 dollars for each offense in addition thereto in the discretion of the court such person may be directed to remove any inscription figure or mark of any type that is painted written or drawn upon any structure  removal of graffiti required  penalty any person who permits graffiti to remain on his or her property for a period of more than seven days after official notification to remove same shall be subject to a fine of 100 dollars  enforcement of article and penalties generally this entire article shall be enforced by the town police department  parks and recreation footnotes  1  charter reference parks commission  1010  recreation commission   cross reference administration ch 2 removal of ice snow from sidewalks a the provisions of a cgs are hereby adopted and are set forth in subsections b c d and e hereof b notwithstanding the provisions of cgs or any other general or special act the town shall not be liable to any person for injury to person or property caused by the presence of ice or snow on a public sidewalk unless the town is the owner or person in possession and control of land abutting such sidewalk other than land used as a highway or street provided that the town shall be liable for its affirmative acts with respect to such sidewalk c the owner or person in possession and control of land abutting a public sidewalk shall have the same duty of care with respect to the presence of ice or snow on such sidewalk toward the portion of the sidewalk abutting his property as the town had prior to the effective date of the ordinance codified in this section and shall be liable to persons injured in person or property where a breach of said duty is the proximate cause of said injury d no action to recover damages for injury to person or property caused by the presence of ice or snow on a public sidewalk against a person who owns or is in possession and control of land abutting a public sidewalk shall be brought but within two years from the date when the injury is first sustained e whenever the public sidewalk shall be wholly or partially covered by snow or ice it shall be the duty of the owner or person in possession and control of land abutting a public sidewalk to cause such sidewalk to be made safe and convenient by removing the snow therefrom within the first six hours of daylight immediately following the accumulation of such snow thereon or in the case of ice by covering the same with sand or other suitable material within the first six hours of daylight following the accumulation of such ice and then renewing such treatment as often as may be necessary to keep such sidewalk safe and convenient in case of the failure or neglect of the owner or person in possession and control of land abutting the public sidewalk to comply with this subsection the selectman may cause the same to be done and the expense thereof shall be collectible from the person so failing or neglecting any person who fails or neglects to comply with this subsection shall also be liable for a penalty or fine in an amount established in accordance with section 19 general penalty     3 cross reference health and sanitation ch 8 acceptance of streets a generally the procedures set forth in this section shall be followed in the acceptance of all streets highways or public ways in the town other than streets of record as of  b conformity to regulations all proposed streets shall be laid out graded and constructed their entire length and full width from street line to street line in full accordance with the following specifications and these regulations and modes of procedure and any amendments thereto c establishment of lines and grades the owner shall engage the services of a registered engineer or surveyor to lay out the lines and grades of the streets their entire width and length d width in accordance with such approved lines and grades the owner shall construct a roadway at least 30 feet wide centered between the street lines in the case of a 50foot highway and at least 36 feet wide in the case of a 60foot highway having a crown of not more than eight inches as the selectmen or their representative may direct no road shall be accepted unless it is at least 50 feet in width e sidewalk shoulders the shoulders of sidewalk areas shall be graded to the centerline grade at the gutter line and have a pitch of not more than onehalf inch to the foot toward said gutter line from the street line the slopes shall start at the street lines f grade the percentage of grade shall not be less than one percent or more than ten percent except that if in the opinion of the selectmen or the zoning and planning commission these limits cause undue hardship they may allow grades in excess of ten percent provided no appreciable hazard to health or safety is thereby created g excavation depth  slope  subgrade all sod and other vegetable matter shall be excavated and stumps removed where fills of less than four feet are made boulders and ledges shall be removed to a depth of at least 12 inches below finished grade slopes in cut or fill shall not be steeper than one on two and shall be neatly graded the subgrade shall be brought to a uniform surface the grade of which shall be inspected and approved by the selectmen or their representative before the surfacing may be done h surfacing upon the proposed subgrade shall be spread a uniform gravel or broken stone surface which shall have a minimum depth after compaction of eight inches except where ledge rock is encountered the depth shall be increased to 12 inches after compaction all surfacing materials shall be approved prior to placing by the selectmen or their representative the finished surface shall be thoroughly compacted by wetting and rolling and shall be uniformly graded to the required crosssection upon this prepared surface there shall be spread a coating of mc1 road oil at the rate of threefourths of a gallon per square yard this coating shall be allowed to set and traffic shall not be allowed to use the roadway until the selectmen or their representative shall have determined that the oil has properly set a seal coat of mc3 road oil shall be applied at the rate of not more than onehalf of a gallon per square yard and shall be immediately covered with clean sand in sufficient quantity to prevent bleeding and picking up of the bitumen before traffic is allowed to use the roadway i storm drains all storm drains determined by the selectmen or their representative to be required by good construction practice and in a manner approved by the selectmen or their representative shall be constructed by the owner or developer at his sole expense the storm drains shall include all necessary pipelines catch basins manholes and appurtenances sufficient and adequate to provide proper drainage wherever in the opinion of the selectmen or their representative the grades will cause excessive erosion and at all catch basins gutters shall be paved with bituminous concrete j inspection and approval during construction the construction on all the above improvements shall always be subject to inspection by the selectmen or their duly appointed representatives no subgrades storm or sanitary sewers drains culverts or bridge work shall be covered until inspected and approved nor shall the gravel surface be oiled until inspected and approved k location monuments reinforced concrete monuments of 4 mix four inches square at the top six inches square at the bottom and three feet long shall be set at angle points points of curve and other critical or control points to define and locate the street rightsofway each monument shall have a brass or iron rod at least six inches long in the top and shall be the point of reference the tops of the monuments shall be set to the established grade the monuments shall be set in place after all other street improvements are completed the accuracy of location of such monuments shall be certified in writing by the land surveyor or engineer making the street layout before the acceptance of such street by the town l final acceptance upon completion of the required improvements as set forth in this section including the setting of all monuments the construction of all roads and the installation of all required drainage facilities and upon certification by the selectmen or their representative of the same in writing the street shall be accepted by the town  acceptance of private roads as public highways no private road may be accepted as a public highway except in accordance with the following provisions 1 compliance with specifications  improvements upon approval of the acceptance of the private road by a town meeting warned for the purpose the abutting owners or developer shall grade surface and drain the private road in accordance with the specifications set forth in section 147  provided however the specifications may be waived by the board of selectmen where compliance would be impracticable or impose undue hardship upon the abutting owners and in such event the town shall make such improvements as shall be necessary to render the highways safe for public travel 2 acceptance upon completion of such improvements certified to the town clerk in writing by the board of selectmen the road shall become a public highway 3 additional standards no private road may become a public highway under this section unless is existed on  and has occupied homes thereon at time of application  deposit of snow or ice on public street forbidden a no person shall plow throw deposit place or cause to be thrown deposited or placed any snow or ice on any public roadway or sidewalk in the town b any owner occupant or person having charge of premises violating any provisions of this section shall be fined in accordance with section 19 of this  street names the board of selectmen shall have the exclusive right to name and rename streets in the town after review of the proposed street names by the emergency permitgenerally a the town engineer is hereby authorized and empowered to grant a permit for excavation or obstruction or substruction of any town roadway subject to the provisions of this article the authorization given by such engineer for such use of the highway shall be in writing in a form prescribed by him which form is designated and known as a permit such permit shall be issued on a engineer may in his discretion extend the time limitation specified in this section or in any other section of this article 3 samerejection of applications when it appears that the work called for in an application required by section 1424 would cause substantial or needless damage to a highway or create excessive disturbance to traffic or exceptionally dangerous conditions not commensurate with the benefits to the applicant the request for such permit may be denied the applicant will be informed of such rejection by letter from the engineer stating the reasons for such rejection the engineer shall reject the application of any person when such applicant has failed to perform work under a previously issued permit within the time required or in the manner required or when the applicant has failed to reimburse the town for recoverable charges billed under the terms governing a previous permit 3 samefees generally  engineers monthly statement the engineer shall collect the sum of $15000 for each permit issued by him under the provisions of this article such sum shall be payable prior to the time the permit is issued all sums of money collected by the engineer shall be paid by him to the town treasurer on a monthly basis the engineer shall submit a monthly statement to the finance department itemizing permit inspection and patching fees collected during the month 3 sametown work no contractor or subcontractor performing work directly for the town or any of its agencies or instrumentalities shall be required to pay any permit fee as provided for in section 1426 3 sameemergency permits generally emergency permits may be granted by the engineer or by the inspector in the case of broken gas or water mains or other such emergencies but the person performing such excavation or creating such obstruction shall file a written application for a permit within 24 hours thereafter in the manner prescribed by this article for nonemergency work 3 sameemergency work when the town or any of its agencies or instrumentalities or any contractor or subcontractor performing work directly for the town or any of its agencies or instrumentalities shall notify the engineer or the inspector that there is immediate need for any excavation or obstruction or in the case of redevelopment construction or demolition that work must be performed immediately the engineer or inspector shall grant an emergency permit as provided in section 1428 3 samerevocation of permit any permit issued by the engineer pursuant to the provisions of this article is revocable immediately upon written notification or oral order given personally to the permittee by the engineer or inspector 3 bond or deposit required it is hereby made the duty of the engineer to determine the amount of the guarantee to be deposited with the town by the permittee in connection with each permit issued pursuant to the provisions of this article he may accept either a certified or bank check or a surety bond with good and sufficient surety such bond to be in a form prescribed by the town counsel no permit shall be issued until such deposit or bond has been filed with the engineer an annual blanket surety bond acceptable to the town counsel may be deposited to avoid the inconvenience and expense of obtaining individual deposits or bonds for each permit requested the engineer shall release such deposit or surety bond six months after the permanent top surface has been installed by either the town or the permit holder  provided however that such deposit or bond shall not be released unless all of the requirements of this article have been met 3 insurance required the applicant for a permit under the provisions of this article shall before issuance of such permit deliver to the town engineer an insurance policy written by an insurance company authorized to do business in this state upon which the town is a named insured which policy shall insure against bodily injury or property damage arising out of any action or activity or work of the applicant in connection with the work undertaken under such permit such policy shall have bodily injury and property damage limits of $100000000 minimum per each occurrence and shall have a $200000000 minimum general aggregate limit 3 time for performance a all work performed under the provisions of this article shall be completed in a manner satisfactory to the engineer before the expiration date established by the engineer which shall be shown on the permit the permit holder may request the engineer to allow an extension of time the extension of time may be granted in writing by the engineer b the inspector shall be notified at least 24 hours in advance of actually starting any work authorized under a permit failure of the permittee to notify the town will result in the revocation of the permit permits are void three months after their issue date 3 inspection the engineer or his agent is empowered to inspect all excavations for workmanship and materials the excavations may not be permanently backfilled without the engineer or his agent ie inspector present at the site the town will require the permittee to excavate and expose for inspection any portion of the excavation backfilled without inspection or authorization to backfill the permittee shall be responsible for the payment of the hourly rate as determined by the engineer of the inspector for the time in which the inspector is observing the backfilling of the excavation an estimate of the required inspectors time will be made and paid for at the time of permit application in the event the actual inspection time exceeds the estimated time the permittee shall pay the additional fee to the town within ten working days failure to pay said additional fee will result in the permittee forfeiting any rights to future permits until the outstanding balance is received the town may at its discretion use the proceeds from the bond required in section 1431 to pay any amounts due to the town in the event that the actual inspection time is less than the estimated time the town will promptly refund any overcharge to the permittee 3 traffic protection it shall be the duty of every permittee under this article to make certain that the security of the travelling public is safeguarded and its rights are not unreasonably curtailed if any excavation or obstruction shall be left upon any highway at night it shall be marked by flares lanterns lights flashing beacons or other warning devices approved by the engineer if the work performed under the highway shall make the travelled portion dangerous for the movement of vehicles a sufficient number of watchmen flagmen or police officers as determined by the traffic authority shall be assigned by the permittee to direct traffic the cost of all watchmen flagmen or police officers shall be the responsibility of the permittee in the event the work of the permittee requires the closing of a public highway for any period of time the permittee shall give written notice to the police department and the director of public works or his designated representative 24 hours in advance of any required closing the director may determine the need for closing the highway and may require the work or work method be so altered so as to provide for traffic flow the town engineer or the director of public works or his agent shall provide written notice to the police and fire departments in advance of closing any public highway any permittee who leaves an excavation in an unsafe condition or abandons a street opening shall be liable for all costs incurred by the town to correct such conditions 3   protection of tree roots the greatest care shall be exercised by persons performing work under the provisions of this article to protect tree roots from damage not only when excavating but on all subsequent operations of construction and backfilling when roots are encountered near the base of a tree the permittee shall tunnel under the roots as directed by the inspector the inspector may require such other protection as shall be reasonable in regard to any particular instance 3   opening of pavement the pavement surface shall be removed with all edges cut to a neat straight line preferably cut with a concrete saw  however such cutting can be accomplished with a spade point tool under no circumstances shall the pavement slab be subject to blows from a hammer or dropweight but any concrete base or subbase under the pavement slab may be broken with a pneumatic tool using a bullpoint 3   size of excavation  placement of excavated material the size of the excavation shall be kept as small as practicable to carry on the work no material removed in excavating shall be placed in the travelled path unless approved by the inspector in any case the material shall be placed so as to interfere as little as possible with the ordinary use of the highway if such excavated material must be placed in gutters suitable conduits first shall be installed temporarily in which to carry drainage beyond the obstruction 3   blasting when rock or other hard material must be removed by a permittee under this article he may blast such material if the pavement or other structures will not be endangered thereby only a blast man licensed by the commissioner of emergency services and public protection will be permitted to charge or set off blasts within the highway rightofway all state and municipal regulations concerning the same shall be fully complied with the permittee shall be responsible for all damage a mat or weight of logs or sand bags shall be placed over the charge to prevent shattered materials from scattering 3   tunneling or jacking tunneling or jacking shall be permitted only when plans prepared by a registered engineer are submitted to and approved by the town engineer 3   backfilling backfill in trenches within paved areas shall be placed in layers not more than 12 inches thick and shall be thoroughly compacted by tamping or other approved means to the satisfaction of the inspector compaction equipment shall be at the excavation site and must be utilized during all backfilling operations the material used for backfill shall be subject to the inspection and approval of the inspector and if in his opinion the excavated material is unsuitable for backfill the permittee shall be required to dispose of the unsuitable materials and replace them with materials that are suitable to the inspector when backfill has been completed within 15 inches of the finished pavement or surface grade the next 14 inches shall be filled and compacted in two seveninch layers using an approved grade of bankrun gravel or processed aggregate 3   temporary patch as soon as the excavation has been backfilled and compacted the pavement shall be replaced temporarily by the permittee the temporary pavement shall consist of bituminous concrete of a mixture approved by the inspector conndot class 2 compressed to a minimum depth of two inches the surface of the temporary pavement shall be flush at the edge of the existing pavement and extend above the surface of the surrounding permanent pavement by one inch in the center of the patch and shall be reasonably smooth the permittee shall be responsible for the temporary pavement and shall see that the contractor or his own forces keep this pavement in repair until the permanent surface can be replaced by the town additional material shall be added by the permittee as necessary as the backfill settles if the permittee does not maintain the temporary pavement adequately the engineer may direct that necessary repairs be made by the department of public works to prevent accidents and the permittee will be charged by the town for this work failure on the part of the town to give notice that repairs are needed shall not relieve the contractor of any of the duties set forth herein 3   permanent patch the permanent repair of street openings shall be the responsibility of the town except in the case of a particularly large or difficult project in which case the engineer may require that the permittee be responsible for installation of the permanent patch the town shall charge each permittee a fee for the cost of said permanent patch based on the area of the final patch as calculated by the engineer the permanent patch shall be a minimum of two feet wider and two feet longer than the temporary patch a permanent patch size will be estimated and paid for at the time of permit application in the event the actual size of the permanent patch exceeds the estimated size of permanent patch the permittee shall pay the additional fee to the town within ten working days failure to pay said additional fees will result in the permittee forfeiting any rights to future permits until the outstanding balance is received the town may at its discretion use the proceeds from the bond required in section 1431 to pay any amounts due to the town in the event that the actual permanent patch is smaller than the estimated size of the permanent patch the town will promptly refund any overcharge to the permittee the unit prices charged for the installation of the permanent patch shall be determined by the engineer in accordance with current costs and construction practices the engineer shall advertise for bids for the permanent patching of town streets in accordance with specifications prepared by the engineer every two years 3   resurfacing when issuing a permit on any highway that has been reconstructed or resurfaced within five years of the date of the permit application the town reserves the right to designate the patch limits and requirements which may include curbtocurb milling and overlay of the affected area plus an additional five feet on each end at a minimum 3   reconstruction of curbs and sidewalks every permittee under the provisions of this article shall reconstruct all curbs and sidewalks disturbed by any excavation made by him with materials similar to those of which they were originally constructed 3   removing manhole covers no person shall remove any manhole cover from any manhole owned or operated by the town without first securing the permission of the engineer to do so 3   termination of permit six months after installation of the temporary patch the permittee shall apply in writing for termination of the permit and release from any obligation involved thereafter if in the opinion of the engineer or his agent the work is not satisfactorily completed or settlement is occurring necessary repairs shall be undertaken by the permittee and an additional period of liability shall be established by the engineer or his agent the installation of a permanent patch by the town to said opening shall terminate the permit and release the permittee from any obligations thereafter 3   penalties any person firm or corporation violating any provision of this article shall be fined not more than $50000 for a first offense and $100000 for each subsequent offense 3   appeals any person firm or corporation aggrieved by the imposition of a fine under section 143513 shall have the right to appeal to the board of selectmen the imposition of said fine in writing the appeal shall state the reasons why the fine should not be imposed the board of selectmens decision in said case shall be final 3 article iii  driveways permit required no construction alteration or repairs shall be performed on any the town 4 the driveway apron shall be paved with at least a two inch layer of class ii bituminous concrete underlayment by at least eight inches of subbase the driveway lip or the vertical rise at the curb line shall be two inches 5 when a driveway crosses a watercourse culvert or other drainage structure designed for at least a 25 year storm shall be provided drainage structures shall be designed and installed to bear a minimum weight of 55000 pounds 6 the following shall apply to driveways serving more than one principal building a the street address of each building served by the driveway shall be indicated by numbers at least three inches high where the driveway meets the town road b the address of each building shall be indicated by numbers at least three inches high affixed to the building c if a common driveway divides the direction to each structure shall be clearly shown at the point of division 7 all phases of work involved in the construction and repair of curbs sidewalks and driveway aprons shall be subject to inspection by the department of public works and the town engineer 8 definitions apron the driveway apron is that portion of a driveway between the takes such action before the tax due date 3 tax exemption for motor vehicles equipped for disabled persons a title this section which shall be known as tax exemption for motor vehicles equipped for disabled persons is adopted pursuant to the provisions of connecticut general statutes  1281c3 b definitions person with disabilities means an individual who has a physical impairment or impairments which substantially limit major life activities such as seeing hearing speaking walking breathing performing manual tasks learning caring for oneself and working however an individual with a minor nonchronic condition or a condition with a short duration shall not be considered to be person with disabilities for the purpose of this ordinance the phrase any motor vehicle owned by a person with disabilities or owned by the parent or guardian of such person which vehicle equipped for purposes of adapting its use to the disability of such person means any vehicle equipped with special hand foot or hand and foot controls wheelchair lifts or hoists or other adaptation to assist physically disabled drivers which is owned by them or their parent or guardian and used by such person with disabilities c motor vehicle tax exemption any motor vehicle which is owned and used by a seymour resident with disabilities or owned by the parent or guardian of such person which is equipped for such disabled person is hereby eligible for exemption from the motor vehicle tax of the town of seymour provided that an application for such exemption is filed with the seymour assessors office in a timely manner pursuant to the provisions of subsection d of this section and the motor vehicle is found by the seymour assessor to satisfy the criteria set forth in this section for such an exemption d procedures for application an applicant for a motor vehicle tax exemption pursuant to this ordinance shall file an application with the assessor annually at any time from the assessment date to within two months after the tax due date said application shall contain all information reasonably required by the assessor to enable him to determine whether or not the applicant and the vehicle satisfy all the requirements set forth in this section the assessor may require the submission of such supplemental information and documentation as he may reasonably require enabling him to determine if the applicant is entitled to said tax exemption the assessor shall determine whether the applicant is eligible for said tax exemption pursuant to the provisions of this section the assessor in making such determination may inspect said motor vehicle and consider the extent to which motor vehicle has been modified the purpose for which the vehicle is being used and the exclusivity of the use of said vehicle failure to file an application for said exemption annually shall result in the loss of the tax exemption but will not preclude any applicant from making application in subsequent years used they shall the meanings respectively ascribed to them in this section alley a public way within a block generally giving access to the rear of lots or buildings and not used for general traffic circulation bicycle every device propelled by human power upon which any person may ride having two tandem wheels either of which is more than 20 inches in diameter board of police commissioners the duly appointed members of the board of police commissioners acting in their official capacity crosswalk that portion of the roadway included within the prolongation of the sidewalk lines at street intersections driver every person who drives or is in actual physical control of a vehicle emergency vehicle police vehicles vehicles of the fire department ambulances vehicles carrying a state or municipal officer or employee in response to an emergency call and emergency vehicles of public service corporations on an emergency call explosive any chemical compound or mechanical mixture that is commonly used or intended for the purpose of producing an explosion and which contains any oxidizing and combustive units or other ingredients in such proportions quantities or packing that an ignition by fire by friction by concussion by percussion or by detonator of any part of the compound or mixture may cause such a sudden generation of highly heated gases that the resultant gaseous pressures are capable of producing destructible effects on contiguous objects or of destroying life or limb farm tractor every motor vehicle designed and used primarily as a farm implement for drawing plows mowing machines and other implements of husbandry improved highway a roadway of concrete brick asphalt macadam or gravel intersection the area embraced within the prolongation of the property lines of two or more streets which join at an angle whether or not such streets cross laned roadway a street the roadway of which is divided into two or more clearly marked lanes for vehicular traffic loading zone the space adjacent to a curb reserved for the exclusive use of vehicles during the loading or unloading of passengers or materials merging traffic a maneuver executed by the drivers of vehicles on converging roadways to permit simultaneous or alternate entry into the junction thereof wherein the driver of each vehicle involved is required to adjust his vehicular speed and lateral position so as to avoid a collision with any other vehicles metal tires every tire the surface of which in contact with the roadway is wholly or partially metal or other hard nonresilient material motorcycle every motor vehicle having a saddle for the use of the rider and designed to travel on not more than three wheels in contact with the ground but excluding a tractor motor vehicle every vehicle which is selfpropelled but not operated upon rails park to stand a vehicle whether occupied or not for a period of time greater than is reasonably necessary for the actual loading or unloading of persons pedestrian any person afoot pneumatic tire every tire in which compressed air is designed to support the load property line the line marking the boundary between any street and lots or property abutting thereon public building a building used by the municipality the county the state or the united states government rightofway the privilege of the immediate use of the roadway road tractor every motor vehicle designed and used for drawing other vehicles and not so constructed as to carry any load thereon either independently or any part of the weight of a vehicle or load so drawn safety zone that portion of a roadway reserved for the exclusive use of pedestrians suitably marked or elevated school bus every motor vehicle operated by or for a public or governmental agency or by or for a private or religious organization solely for the transportation of pupils in connection with school activities semitrailer every vehicle without motive power designed for carrying persons or property and for being drawn by a motor vehicle and so constructed that some part of its weight and that of its load rests upon or is carried by another vehicle sidewalk that portion of a air for the support of the load street or highway the entire width between property lines or every way or place of whatever nature when any part thereof is open to the use of the public as a matter of right for the purpose of vehicular traffic traffic pedestrians ridden or herded animals vehicles and other conveyances whether singly or together while using any highway for the purpose of travel vehicle truck tractor every motor vehicle designed and used primarily for drawing other vehicles and not so constructed as to carry a load other than a part of the weight of the vehicle and load so
